  <title>
   College Football Recruiting Prediction Model
  </title>
  <style>

  <p align="center">
   <a href="http://www2.mercer.edu/Business/default.htm">
    <img border="0" height="113" src="lynch/Mercer%20WordmarkSSBE%20-%20small-medium.jpg" width="389"/>
   </a>
  </p>
  <p align="center">
   <b>
    <font face="Arial" size="5">
     College Football 
			Recruiting Prediction Model
    </font>
   </b>
  </p>
  <p align="center" style="margin-bottom: 20px">
   <a href="http://www.sas.com/">
    <img border="0" height="32" src="lynch/powered_stat.gif" vspace="10" width="92"/>
   </a>
  </p>
  <div align="center">
   <table border="1" bordercolor="#FFFFFF" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="MsoNormalTable" height="2063" style="width: 1230px; border-collapse: collapse; margin-left: 4.65pt">
    <tr>
     <td bgcolor="#C0C0C0" height="10" nowrap="" style="width: 592px; padding-left: 5.4pt; padding-right: 5.4pt; padding-top: 0in; padding-bottom: 0in; border-right-style:none; border-right-width:medium" valign="bottom">
     </td>
     <td align="center" bgcolor="#C0C0C0" height="8" nowrap="" style="border-style:none; border-width:medium; padding-left: 5.4pt; padding-right: 5.4pt; padding-top: 0in; padding-bottom: 0in" valign="bottom" width="607">
      <p style="margin-top: 5px; margin-bottom: 5px">
       <b>
        <font face="Arial">
         Predictions for the Top 
						Recruits
        </font>
       </b>
       <b>
        <font face="Arial">
         as of
         <!--webbot bot="Timestamp" S-Type="EDITED" S-Format="%B %d, %Y" startspan -->
         February 05, 2009
         <!--webbot bot="Timestamp" i-checksum="41413" endspan -->
        </font>
       </b>
      </p>
     </td>
    </tr>
    <tr>
     <td bgcolor="#FFFFFF" rowspan="2" style="border-left:medium none #FFFFFF; border-bottom:medium none #FFFFFF; padding-left: 5.4pt; padding-right: 5.4pt; padding-top: 0in; padding-bottom: 0in; border-right-style:none; border-right-width:medium; border-top-style:none; border-top-width:medium" valign="top" width="592">
      <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 6.6pt">
       <span style="font-size: 10.0pt; font-family: Arial; background: white">
        Welcome to the college football recruiting prediction 
						model website hosted by the
        <a href="http://www2.mercer.edu/Business/default.htm" style="color: blue; text-decoration: underline; text-underline: single">
         Stetson School of Business and Economics
        </a>
        at
        <a href="http://www2.mercer.edu/default.htm" style="color: blue; text-decoration: underline; text-underline: single">
         Mercer University
        </a>
        . This website contains 
						information about an econometric model that has been 
						developed by three economists (Mike DuMond, Allen Lynch 
						and Jennifer Platania) to predict the collegiate choices 
						of high school football players.
       </span>
      </p>
      <p class="MsoNormal">
       <span style="font-size: 10.0pt; font-family: Arial; background: white">
       </span>
      </p>
      <p class="MsoNormal">
       <span style="font-size: 10.0pt; font-family: Arial; background: white">
        Each year, on the first Wednesday in February, college 
						coaches, administrators, and football fans eagerly await 
						the choices of high school seniors as they sign letters 
						of intent with specific colleges. These letters of 
						intent officially link top ranked high school football 
						players with specific colleges and effectively determine 
						the rosters of college football programs in years to 
						come. The process of recruiting these players is highly 
						competitive, as schools battle with one another to sign 
						the best of the best in the world of high school 
						football. Recruiting gurus attempt to forecast the 
						choices of these high school athletes as college 
						football fans desperately search the Internet for bits 
						and pieces of information that might shed light on the 
						choices of these teenage football players.
       </span>
      </p>
      <p class="MsoNormal">
       <span style="font-size: 10.0pt; font-family: Arial; background: white">
       </span>
      </p>
      <p class="MsoNormal">
       <span style="font-size: 10.0pt; font-family: Arial; background: white">
        The importance to a specific college of signing a strong 
						group of athletes on signing day cannot be overstated. 
						College football has become big business in recent 
						years. The amount of revenue a college or university 
						can generate by fielding a competitive football team can 
						reach staggering levels. The college football program 
						at the University of Texas at Austin, for example, brought in 
						over $53 million
       </span>
       <a href="lynch/#_ftn1" style="color: blue; text-decoration: underline; text-underline: single" title="">
        <span class="MsoFootnoteReference">
         <span style="font-size: 10.0pt; font-family: Arial; color: windowtext; text-decoration: none; background: white">
          [1]
         </span>
        </span>
       </a>
       <span style="font-size: 10.0pt; font-family: Arial; background: white">
        during the 2004-2005 academic year. Given the potential 
						for such revenue, as well as the general interest in the 
						sport held by rabid college football fans, an 
						econometric model to predict the choices of college 
						becomes useful.
       </span>
      </p>
      <p class="MsoNormal">
       <span style="font-size: 10.0pt; font-family: Arial; background: white">
       </span>
      </p>
      <p class="MsoNormal">
       <span style="font-size: 10.0pt; font-family: Arial; background: white">
        The authors used statistical software developed by
        <a href="http://www.sas.com/" style="color: blue; text-decoration: underline; text-underline: single">
         SAS
        </a>
        along with data provided by
        <a href="http://www.rivals.com/" style="color: blue; text-decoration: underline; text-underline: single">
         Rivals.com
        </a>
        (a national website dedicated to college 
						football and recruiting) in the development of this 
						model. The model was built on a database capturing 
						characteristics and decisions of 3,395 recruited 
						athletes for the three recruiting seasons between 2002 
						and 2004. On average, each player was choosing from 
						among a group of 4 schools. A wide array of player and 
						team level data were gathered for this task. Then, a 
						special form of a probit model was developed to capture, 
						to the best extent possible a statistical equation to 
						capture the decision making process.
       </span>
      </p>
      <p class="MsoNormal">
       <span style="font-size: 10.0pt; font-family: Arial; background: white">
       </span>
      </p>
      <p class="MsoNormal">
       <span style="font-size: 10.0pt; font-family: Arial; background: white">
        We were a bit surprised by the results. There were a 
						number of factors that we thought would significantly 
						impact the decision of the high school athlete that 
						didnt. For example, factors like the schools 
						graduation rate, the number of Bowl Championship Series 
						(BCS) bowl appearances, the current roster depth at the 
						recruited players position, the number of players from 
						a specific college drafted by the NFL, and even the 
						number of national championships won by a particular 
						program dont systematically influence the decisions of 
						high school athletes. Surprised? So were we. What, 
						then, does matter? As it turns out the following 
						factors DO significantly impact the decision of high 
						school athletes:
       </span>
      </p>
      <p class="MsoNormal">
       <span style="font-size: 10.0pt; font-family: Arial; background: white">
       </span>
      </p>
      <ul style="margin-top: 0in; margin-bottom: 0in" type="disc">
       <li class="MsoNormal">
        <span style="font-size: 10.0pt; font-family: Arial; background: white">
         Whether the athlete made an official visit to a 
							specific college
        </span>
       </li>
       <li class="MsoNormal">
        <span style="font-size: 10.0pt; font-family: Arial; background: white">
         Whether the school is in a BCS 
							conference
        </span>
       </li>
       <li class="MsoNormal">
        <span style="font-size: 10.0pt; font-family: Arial; background: white">
         The distance from the high school athletes hometown 
							to a specific school
        </span>
       </li>
       <li class="MsoNormal">
        <span style="font-size: 10.0pt; font-family: Arial; background: white">
         Whether the recruit is in the same state as a 
							specific school
        </span>
       </li>
       <li class="MsoNormal">
        <span style="font-size: 10.0pt; font-family: Arial; background: white">
         The final AP Ranking of a specific school in the 
							previous year of competition
        </span>
       </li>
       <li class="MsoNormal">
        <span style="font-size: 10.0pt; font-family: Arial; background: white">
         The number of conference titles a school has 
							recorded in recent years
        </span>
       </li>
       <li class="MsoNormal">
        <span style="font-size: 10.0pt; font-family: Arial; background: white">
         Whether the school is currently under a bowl ban 
							for violating NCAA rules
        </span>
       </li>
       <li class="MsoNormal">
        <span style="font-size: 10.0pt; font-family: Arial; background: white">
         The current number of scholarship reductions a 
							school faces for violating NCAA rules
        </span>
       </li>
       <li class="MsoNormal">
        <span style="font-size: 10.0pt; font-family: Arial; background: white">
         The size of the teams stadium (measured in terms of 
							seating capacity)
        </span>
       </li>
       <li class="MsoNormal">
        <span style="font-size: 10.0pt; font-family: Arial; background: white">
         Whether the school has an on-campus 
							stadium
        </span>
       </li>
       <li class="MsoNormal">
        <span style="font-size: 10.0pt; font-family: Arial; background: white">
         The current age of the teams 
							stadium
        </span>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p class="MsoNormal">
       <span style="font-size: 10.0pt; font-family: Arial; background: white">
       </span>
      </p>
      <p class="MsoNormal">
       <span style="font-size: 10.0pt; font-family: Arial; background: white">
        So, in a nutshell, high school athletes prefer winning 
						programs that are
        <br/>
        close to home, are in possession of good physical 
						facilities, and are in good
        <br/>
        graces with the NCAA. Interestingly enough however, 
						reduced scholarships
        <i>
         increase
        </i>
        the likelihood of 
						choosing a particular school, holding all else constant. 
						This is likely because reduced scholarships imply 
						reduced competition for exposure and playing time in the 
						future.
       </span>
      </p>
      <p class="MsoNormal">
      </p>
      <p class="MsoNormal">
       <span style="-moz-background-clip: initial; -moz-background-origin: initial; -moz-background-inline-policy: initial; font-size: 10pt; font-family: Arial; background: white 0% 50%">
        Does the model predict accurately? We believe the model 
					predicts quite accurately! Within the sample used to build 
					the model, we accurately predicted approximately 68 percent 
					of the choices of high school athletes. (Considering that 
					each player was choosing from a group of, on average, four 
					schools, a 68 percent accuracy rate isn't too bad.) In 
					2005, we examined the choices of the top 100 high school 
					prospects and used the model to accurately predict the 
					choices of 71 of these players. After a brief hiatus in 
					2006 we came back with more predictions in 2007. For the 
					top 100 of the 2007 recruiting class, the model accurately 
					predicted the decisions of 72. Making the accuracy rate of 
					the 2007 class more impressive is the fact that each player 
					in the 2007 class was choosing from an average of 6.2 
					schools! In 2008, the model accurately predicted the 
					choices of 73% of the Top 250 recruits in the land.
       </span>
      </p>
      <p>
       <span style="-moz-background-clip: initial; -moz-background-origin: initial; -moz-background-inline-policy: initial; font-size: 10pt; font-family: Arial; background: white 0% 50%">
        Information regarding the predicted and actual choices for 
					the top 250 recruits of 2009 (as determined by Rivals.com) 
					appears to the right. Also to the right, the potential 
					schools and associated probabilities, as determined by the 
					results of the model, for the recruits in this group that 
					have yet to decide are listed. Of the
        <span lang="en-us">
         245
        </span>
        athletes that 
					have made predictions, we have accurately pegged the 
					decisions of 1
        <span lang="en-us">
         74
        </span>
        , translating into a 7
        <span lang="en-us">
         1
        </span>
        % accuracy rate.
       </span>
       <span style="font-size: 10.0pt; font-family: Arial; background: white">
       </span>
      </p>
      <p class="MsoNormal">
       <span style="font-size: 10.0pt; font-family: Arial; background: white">
        The results of this model appear in an article published 
						in the February, 2008 edition of
        <a href="http://jse.sagepub.com/" style="color: blue; text-decoration: underline; text-underline: single">
         The Journal of Sports Economics
        </a>
        . The recruiting 
						prediction model is the subject of a current article 
						authored by Andy Staples in Sports Illustrated (
        <a href="http://sportsillustrated.cnn.com/2008/writers/andy_staples/01/23/recruiting.economics/index.html" style="color: blue; text-decoration: underline; text-underline: single">
         link
        </a>
        ). 
						Additionally, separate media stories regarding the 
						results of the model have appeared in the
        <a href="http://www.columbusdispatch.com/live/contentbe/dispatch/2007/02/06/20070206-E2-03.html" style="color: blue; text-decoration: underline; text-underline: single">
         Columbus Dispatch
        </a>
        , the Atlanta Journal-Constitution 
						and via an Associated Press article written by Paul 
						Nowell in 2005.
       </span>
      </p>
      <p class="MsoNormal">
       <span style="font-size: 10.0pt; font-family: Arial; background: white">
       </span>
      </p>
      <p class="MsoNormal">
       <span style="font-size: 10.0pt; font-family: Arial; background: white">

        </a>

						collection of GIS related data. The authors would also

        </a>
        for web site development and support.
       </span>
      </p>
      <p class="MsoNormal">
      </p>
      <p class="MsoNormal">

      </p>
      <p class="MsoNormal">

      </p>

       <span lang="en-us">

       </a>
       is Associate Professor of Economics 
						and Quantitative Methods in the
       <a href="http://www2.mercer.edu/Business/default.htm" style="color: blue; text-decoration: underline; text-underline: single">
        Stetson School of Business and Economics
       </a>

       <a href="http://www2.mercer.edu/default.htm" style="color: blue; text-decoration: underline; text-underline: single">

       </a>

       <a href="mailto:jplatania@elon.edu" style="color: blue; text-decoration: underline; text-underline: single">

       </a>

       </a>

      </span>

      <p style="margin-top: 5px; margin-bottom: 5px">
       <span lang="en-us">
        <font face="Arial">
         Currently, the 
						model is predicting at a 71% accuracy rate for the 
						committed players.
        </font>
